Building a web scraper for international rugby scoring

Published: Thu 04 January 2018
By John Boudreaux

In General.

tags: Rugby Sports Web Scraper

Rugby Stats Web Scraper¶

ESPN has a database of all international rugby scores, back to before the 1950s. Using Jupyter notebooks, I wanted to go through the basic steps of building a web scraper to get this data into a more friendly format (.csv) so that I can do more analysis with it in Python or R. This web scraper is built using Python and BeautifulSoup. Let's start by taking a look at the URL of a relevant query of the last 10 years worth of international data.

URL: http://stats.espnscrum.com/statsguru/rugby/stats/index.html?class=1;page=;spanmax1=08+Nov+2017;spanmax2=08+Nov+2017;spanmin1=08+Nov+2007;spanmin2=08+Nov+2015;spanval1=span;spanval2=span;template=results;type=player;view=match

We can define empty arrays that we'll store all our values in for later. Also, we should go ahead and import relevant libraries to start.

In [1]:
import time
from datetime import datetime
from bs4 import BeautifulSoup
import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
import urllib


###all of the variables that we'll be importing
player_list = []
country_list = []
position_list = []
points_list = []
tries_list = []
conv_list = []
pens_list = []
drops_list = []
result_list = []
opp_list = []

print('libraries successfully imported')

libraries successfully imported

With that out of the way, now we can get to the actual scraper. Let's define a string, that we can iterate through for each individual page for all the pages. There were 1601 pages the last time I checked.

In [2]:
def table_url_page(page):
	return('http://stats.espnscrum.com/statsguru/rugby/stats/index.html?class=1;page=' + str(page) +
	';spanmax1=08+Nov+2017;spanmax2=08+Nov+2017;spanmin1=08+Nov+2007;spanmin2=08+Nov+2015;' + 
	'spanval1=span;spanval2=span;template=results;type=player;view=match')

For the sake of this being an example, I'll only do one page. But to create this into a web scraper to get information from all 1061 pages, you would simply need to iterate over all the page numbers and store the values in the arrays we defined in cell 1. It would also be good practice to have a slight delay between each iteration, to not create too many requests at one time.

But let's go ahead and start with the first page, page 1.

In [3]:
page = 1

with urllib.request.urlopen(table_url_page(page)) as url:
    s = url.read()

soup = BeautifulSoup(s)
print(soup)

So that's all the code that our web browser is interpreting when we see that page- and it's a lot. If you go through it about midway down, you start seeing things like country names, numbers, and player names- that's the stuff we want. With BeautifulSoup, we can filter through everything else around it by explicitly telling it what brackets (<>stuff we're looking for) to look for. We'll start off by looking at all of the items in the  tag, since it looks like all of the data is contained there in the "data1" class.





In [4]:


table_entries = soup.find_all("tr", class_="data1")
print(table_entries)

Well, that got rid of a lot of the code we didn't really care about nicely. What's left looks like the table that we wanted to get information from. Why don't we go ahead and count the number of entries on each page too...





In [5]:


entries_on_page = len(table_entries)
print(entries_on_page)









50










So we have 50 data entries- that's a little big for an example. We'll go about making sure that we accurately scrape the first 3 entries, because we can easily change 3 to 50 if we have it all correct. If we look at the the result from box 4, we can see what tags are around the data we want to grab, and use BeautifulSoup to get the text out of there for us. Let's start with getting the player name from the first entry.





In [6]:


i = 1
entry = table_entries[i]
player = entry.find("a", class_="data-link").get_text()
player = str(player)
print(player)









A Goromaru










Got it, just how we wanted it. Now we can repeat for all the fields we care about.





In [7]:


i = 1
entry = table_entries[i]

player = entry.find("a", class_="data-link").get_text()
player = str(player)

country = entry.find("i").get_text()
country = str(country)
##get rid of parentheses around country abbreviation
country = country.replace("(", "")
country = country.replace(")", "")

position = entry.find_all("td", class_="left")[1].get_text()
position = str(position)

points_scored = entry.find("b").get_text()
points_scored = str(points_scored)

tries_scored = entry.find_all("td")[3].get_text()
tries_scored = str(tries_scored)

conversions_scored = entry.find_all("td")[4].get_text()
conversions_scored = str(conversions_scored)

penalties_scored = entry.find_all("td")[5].get_text()
penalties_scored = str(penalties_scored)

drops_scored = entry.find_all("td")[6].get_text()
drops_scored = str(drops_scored)

result = entry.find_all("td", class_="left")[2].get_text()
result = str(result)

opposition = entry.find_all("td", class_="left")[3].get_text()
opposition = str(opposition)
opposition = opposition.replace("v ", "")

print("This was entry number %d" %i)
print("Player is " + player)
print("Country is " + country)
print("Position is " + position)
print("Scored " + points_scored + " points")
print("Scored " + tries_scored + " tries")
print("Scored " + conversions_scored + " conversions")
print("Scored " + penalties_scored + " pens") 
print("Scored " + drops_scored + " drop goals")
print("Result of game was " + result)
print("The opposition was " + opposition)

Player is A Goromaru
Country is JPN
Position is FB
Scored 36 points
Scored 1 tries
Scored 14 conversions
Scored 1 pens
Scored 0 drop goals
Result of game was won
The opposition was Philippines










Perfect. Now if we throw this in a loop, we'll be able to get all the entries on the page. But for the sake of being concise, we'll do only 3 and print the results.





In [8]:


for i in range(len(range(1,3+1))):

    entry = table_entries[i]
    player = entry.find("a", class_="data-link").get_text()
    player = str(player)

    country = entry.find("i").get_text()
    country = str(country)
    ##get rid of parentheses around country abbreviation
    country = country.replace("(", "")
    country = country.replace(")", "")

    position = entry.find_all("td", class_="left")[1].get_text()
    position = str(position)

    points_scored = entry.find("b").get_text()
    points_scored = str(points_scored)

    tries_scored = entry.find_all("td")[3].get_text()
    tries_scored = str(tries_scored)

    conversions_scored = entry.find_all("td")[4].get_text()
    conversions_scored = str(conversions_scored)

    penalties_scored = entry.find_all("td")[5].get_text()
    penalties_scored = str(penalties_scored)

    drops_scored = entry.find_all("td")[6].get_text()
    drops_scored = str(drops_scored)

    result = entry.find_all("td", class_="left")[2].get_text()
    result = str(result)

    opposition = entry.find_all("td", class_="left")[3].get_text()
    opposition = str(opposition)
    opposition = opposition.replace("v ", "")

    print("This was entry number %d" %(i+1))
    print("Player is " + player)
    print("Country is " + country)
    print("Position is " + position)
    print("Scored " + points_scored + " points")
    print("Scored " + tries_scored + " tries")
    print("Scored " + conversions_scored + " conversions")
    print("Scored " + penalties_scored + " pens") 
    print("Scored " + drops_scored + " drop goals")
    print("Result of game was " + result)
    print("The opposition was " + opposition)
    print("")

Country is JPN
Position is FB
Scored 37 points
Scored 1 tries
Scored 16 conversions
Scored 0 pens
Scored 0 drop goals
Result of game was won
The opposition was Sri Lanka

We now have the framework of what we need to do in order to create a csv. All we need to do is loop for all the table entries on the page, within a larger loop of going through all the pages. We can store each entry as an item in an array, and then create a data frame using pandas. We can then call .to_csv and we'll have our data frame.
With the next post, I'll go into a little bit of analysis of the stats of what we have after all this web scraping.
